style="line-height:120%;padding-top:12px;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;font-weight:bold;">(e) Grant of awards to certain named executive officers under the Cash Performance Unit Plan for the 2014-2016 performance cycle.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:6px;text-align:left;text-indent:30px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">On February 12, 2014, the Compensation Committee (the "Committee") of the Board of Directors of McDonald's Corporation (the "Company") approved awards to executives under the Cash Performance Unit Plan ("CPUP") for the performance period from January&#160;1, 2014 to December&#160;31, 2016 ("2014 CPUP").</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:12px;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">CPUP operates on a three-year cycle with a cumulative payout at the end of the cycle based on the entire performance period.&#160;Participants will not receive any payout under the 2014 CPUP until after the end of the performance period on December&#160;31, 2016. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:12px;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">The performance measures that will be used to calculate 2014 CPUP payouts are:</font></div><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="padding-top:12px;font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:48px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;padding-left:24px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Consolidated three-year compounded annual growth in operating income (weighted 75%), which reflects growth in income from all company-operated and franchised restaurants.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="padding-top:12px;font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:48px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Three-year return on incremental invested capital (weighted 25%).</font></div></td></tr></table><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:5pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:5pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:6px;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Participants will not receive any payout under 2014 CPUP unless threshold levels of both performance measures are achieved.&#160;To calculate the final payout, the amount based on the above performance measures will be adjusted by a multiplier based on the Company&#8217;s cumulative total shareholder return versus the S&amp;P 500 Index for the performance period, which may result in final payouts being increased or decreased by up to 15%.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:12px;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Target 2014 CPUP awards for the Company's "named executive officers" for through December&#160;31, 2016.&#160;The EPS target approved by the Committee for the RSUs is&#160;6% compounded annual EPS growth on a cumulative basis.&#160;If no&#160;EPS growth is achieved, none of the RSUs will vest. If EPS growth is positive,&#160;but below this cumulative 6% target, a portion of the awards will vest in proportion to the level of EPS growth achieved, as established by the Committee.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:12px;text-align:left;text-indent:30px;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">For compensation purposes, EPS is&#160;adjusted from the&#160;measures as&#160;reported in our financial statements. Specifically,&#160;EPS&#160;is expressed in constant currencies (i.e., excluding the effects of foreign currency translation) to more accurately reflect underlying business trends.&#160;In addition,
